  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e4baf1a7-d5dd-4323-8e74-3fa750527b5d'
      });

  <span id="freeText5150338644164312214" style="display:none"><b>What would make the perfect man?</b> <p> That's the deliciously racy topic that Jaine Bright and her three girlfriends are pondering one night at their favorite after-hours hot spot: Mr. Perfect. Would he be tall, dark, and handsome? Caring and warmhearted -- or will just muscular do? As their conversation heats up, they concoct a tongue-in-cheek checklist that becomes an overnight sensation, spreading like wildfire at work and sizzling along e-mail lines. But what began as a joke among friends turns deadly serious when one of the four women is murdered....Turning to her neighbor, an unpredictable police detective, for help, Jaine must unmask a killer to save her friends -- and herself. Now, knowing whom to trust and whom to love is a matter of survival -- as the dream of Mr. Perfect becomes a chilling nightmare.</p></span>

I'm not much for that either but the mystery part was intriguing. I would pr<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Some pretty racy scenes, although that's not the main focus of the story. I'm not much for that either but the mystery part was intriguing. I would probably say to skip if you are worried about inappropriate content. Hope that helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer314929582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer187666783170456193"><b><br/>Dear book:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385379855ra/7136822.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><br/>This is my favorite Linda Howard so far <3<br/><br/>I enjoyed every second of it, laughed like crazy at half the book and swooned over Sam the other half of it :D<br/><br/><br/><br/><blockquote><i>“Let me go,” she said, more nervous than she cared to reveal.<br/>“No.”<br/>“No!” she repeated. “You can’t say no. It’s against the law to hold me against my will.”<br/>“I’m not holding you against your will; I’m holding you against your car.”</i></blockquote>
<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>The story</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385380746i/7136967.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>Four friends meet for lunch and make a fun list about what a perfect man should be like.<br/>That, of cou</span>
  <span id="freeText187666783170456193" style="display:none"><b><br>Dear book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385379855ra/7136822.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br>This is my favorite Linda Howard so far &lt;3<br><br>I enjoyed every second of it, laughed like crazy at half the book and swooned over Sam the other half of it :D<br><br><br><br><blockquote><i>“Let me go,” she said, more nervous than she cared to reveal.<br>“No.”<br>“No!” she repeated. “You can’t say no. It’s against the law to hold me against my will.”<br>“I’m not holding you against your will; I’m holding you against your car.”</i></blockquote>
<br><br><br><br><br>The story</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385380746i/7136967.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Four friends meet for lunch and make a fun list about what a perfect man should be like.<br>That, of course, goes public and makes a lot of problems with them, especially when a psycho lunatic finds himself insulted by their requirements and decides to punish them all.<br><br><br>This was fun though I don't think it would've gotten so big in real life (the list and all the hype around it), but who cares ahahhah :D<br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I changed my mind.” She was still pushing on his shoulders. She was still accomplishing exactly nothing.<br>“You can’t change your mind!” He sounded desperate now.<br>“Yes, I can.”<br>“Do you have herpes?”<br>“No.”<br>“Syphilis?”<br>“No.”<br>“Gonorrhea?”<br>“No.”<br>“AIDS?”<br>“No!”<br>“Then you can’t change your mind.”<br>“What I have is a ripe egg.” That was probably a lie. Almost positively a lie. She would probably start her period tomorrow, so the little ovum was long past viability, but she didn’t take chances with potential offspring. If any life was left in the bundle of DNA, Sam’s sperm would jump-start it. Some things were just a given.<br>The ripe-egg news gave him pause. He thought about it. Offered: “I can use a condom.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><b>Sam and Jaine</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385380746ra/7136968.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The romance here was so fun and the attraction between them amazing!<br>They were a mix of love and hate and that's what made it awesome :D<br>They fought all the time and flirted all the time and I just loved it all &lt;3<br>One thing though that didn't make sense and I have to say I've noticed LH has a tendency to do insta-love in her books, but here it went a bit too far...<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the marriage proposal was way too soon for my taste, didn't make sense at all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>That's basically the only thing I didn't like in this book but I looked past it because everything else was perfect :)<br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I didn’t shake you. I kind of bounced on you, but I didn’t shake you.”<br>“Bounced,” he repeated.<br>“You had a hard-on. I couldn’t let it go to waste, could I?”<br>“You could have woke me up before you started not letting it go to waste.”<br>“Look,” she said, exasperated, “if you don’t want it used, don’t lie on your back with it sticking up like that. If that isn’t an invitation, I don’t know what is.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><br><br><b>Overall</b><br><br>Mucho love for this one &lt;3<br>The romance &lt;3<br>The dialogue &lt;3<br>The fights &lt;3<br>The humor &lt;3<br><br>Oh and I forgot, the bad guy! I totally didn't see it coming when it was revealed who it was. Maybe I'm just that stupid but oh well, it was a surprise and I'm happy I didn't guess right :D<br><br><br><b>For anyone who hasn't tried LH and would want to, you can start with this one, or After the Night if you like jerkish heroes :D</b><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_933745914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933745914" />
    <a title="Corina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8905971-corina"><img alt="Corina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580618612p2/8905971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933745914?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corina" href="/user/show/8905971-corina">Corina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=jerk">jerk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933745914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18195575832134364230">THERE ARE MULTIPLE REASONS WHY I LOVE THIS BOOK….<br/><br/>A) THE BANTER<br/><br/>B) THE CHEMISTRY<br/><br/>I can’t count anymore how often this book made me laugh out loud. The dialogues between Sam and Jaine are on point, funny, sexy, hilarious. Janie is such a straightforward kind of person, she attacks life with gusto, and tenacity. She is not afraid of anything, and it shows. Sam, the poor guy, should be afraid, but he is the opposite, he loves everything about Jaine. He is confident, unfazed, and perfectly equipped to </span>
  <span id="freeText18195575832134364230" style="display:none">THERE ARE MULTIPLE REASONS WHY I LOVE THIS BOOK….<br /><br />A) THE BANTER<br /><br />B) THE CHEMISTRY<br /><br />I can’t count anymore how often this book made me laugh out loud. The dialogues between Sam and Jaine are on point, funny, sexy, hilarious. Janie is such a straightforward kind of person, she attacks life with gusto, and tenacity. She is not afraid of anything, and it shows. Sam, the poor guy, should be afraid, but he is the opposite, he loves everything about Jaine. He is confident, unfazed, and perfectly equipped to handle a strong-willed woman like Jaine, and it shows in many ways throughout the novel. And he is never in danger of losing sight of what’s important, and the way he takes care of Jaine is still my favorite part of the book.<br /><br />Together they were explosive. And I had a first row seat, enjoying it all.<br /><br />Also their easy way with each other, their no-nonsense approach to a future relationship was refreshing, and so Linda Howard. Now, reading this book in 2019, I realize that there is a hefty dose of insta-marriage in this book. I’m trying to remember if this was the norm in 2000. I’m not usually a fan of insta-anything, but the overall feel of this novel is still the same as it was when I read it the first time.<br /><br />The suspense is through the roof, and I’m actually shocked every time about the author not pulling any punches. There is quite the body count in this novel. I feel like this rarely happens in romantic suspense novels anymore. And it surprises me every time I read it.<br /><br />So, if you love romantic suspense you MUST read Linda Howard’s books, but especially this one.<br /><br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br /><a href="https://thebrowneyedbookworm.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more reviews and book recommendations on my blog</a><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebrowneyedbookworm/" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Bookstagram</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18195575832134364230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131460108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131460108" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131460108?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a romance with elements of both comedy and danger</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=made-me-laugh">made-me-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=suspense-or-thriller">suspense-or-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131460108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9696900201872417139"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"If you're looking for Mr. Perfect, you're going to spend your whole life being disappointed, because he doesn't exist."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341607i/697683.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I generally hate books where any female or group of females start making a mental or physical list of what they want in a man. Lists are absolutely stupid. Love is unpredictable and shouldn't be put in a box. Sure, six-pack abs and a huge salary can be awesome, but the sweet guy with the messy hair and cute dimples might be the right one, even if he doesn't have gun</span>
  <span id="freeText9696900201872417139" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"If you're looking for Mr. Perfect, you're going to spend your whole life being disappointed, because he doesn't exist."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341607i/697683.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I generally hate books where any female or group of females start making a mental or physical list of what they want in a man. Lists are absolutely stupid. Love is unpredictable and shouldn't be put in a box. Sure, six-pack abs and a huge salary can be awesome, but the sweet guy with the messy hair and cute dimples might be the right one, even if he doesn't have guns of steel or a six figure income.<br><br>Whoops. Let me get off my soap box because this wasn't <i>that</i> type of book. On the contrary, the list was supposed to be a fun game and nothing more, which made me thankful that I wasn't going to have to hate the characters in this book for being ultra-shallow.<br><br><i>Mr. Perfect</i> is a romantic suspense/murder mystery book with a side of comedy. Suspense is not my preferred genre, and cops are not my preferred type of hero, but Linda Howard surprised me by making both work in her favor because I ended up really liking this book!<br><br>It must have been that side of comedy which made the book feel like it wasn't as somber as it could have been.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>Computer Nerd office signs for the win!</b><br><br>XEROX AND WURLITZER HAVE ANNOUNCED THEY WILL MERGE TO MARKET REPRODUCTIVE ORGANS.<br><br>NEW PRESS RELEASE BY THE FDA : RED MEAT IS NOT BAD FOR YOU. RESULTS OF TESTS SHOW IT IS FUZZY GREEN MEAT THAT IS BAD FOR YOU.</blockquote><br>These signs sprinkled throughout the book, along with some of the fun banter, brought a great balance to the dark subject matter.<br><br>After all, there was still a killer on the loose, terrorizing the four women who started the list. Looks like someone didn't feel perfect enough to make the list...<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Which one are you?" whispered a ghostly voice.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I mentioned the cop hero. Sam was great. Who knew I just needed the right author to come along and make me fall for a cop? He might have been a little too gruff at times and made a few off remarks (yes, he called his ex-wife a bitch) which you might not see in a more recent novel, but when he needed to be, he was sweet and protective.<br><br>There were a couple of little pokes at feminism which were odd, but I sort of rolled right over them because I wasn't seeing any big malice showing through. In fact, I didn't have much to complain about when it came to <i>Mr. Perfect</i>. Between the mystery, the romance, and the comedy, I got enough to keep me entertained on a lazy night. If I had to come up with one complaint it would have to be hidden behind a spoiler tag, so only look if you don't mind being spoiled. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A marriage proposal and declarations of love during sex? Really? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I'll definitely pick up another Linda Howard book again in the future, if only to get my fix of random wacky lines such as :<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Then I got inside you and it was like sticking my cock in an electrical outlet."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="9696900201872417139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196880240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196880240" />
    <a title="Wicked Incognito Now" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now"><img alt="Wicked Incognito Now" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1337228064p2/541201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196880240?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wicked Incognito Now" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wicked Incognito Now" href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now">Wicked Incognito Now</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11725217-mr-perfect">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/541201-wicked-incognito-now?shelf=so-irritating">so-irritating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/541201-wicked-incognito-now?shelf=over-rated">over-rated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/541201-wicked-incognito-now?shelf=fluff">fluff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/541201-wicked-incognito-now?shelf=dnf-super-totally-awful">dnf-super-totally-awful</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196880240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9045131196174131044">I only read SEVEN PERCENT of this book. So take my review with a grain of salt.<br/><br/>I often search the internet for "best romance novels of all time." There are, surprisingly, a lot of lists dedicated to enumerating the best romance novels ever written. I've found quite a few gems this way. THIS novel made the top ten of most of those lists. I spent most of my life thinking that all romance novels were a waste of my time and intellect, until I rediscovered romance about four years ago. I discovered t</span>
  <span id="freeText9045131196174131044" style="display:none">I only read SEVEN PERCENT of this book. So take my review with a grain of salt.<br /><br />I often search the internet for "best romance novels of all time." There are, surprisingly, a lot of lists dedicated to enumerating the best romance novels ever written. I've found quite a few gems this way. THIS novel made the top ten of most of those lists. I spent most of my life thinking that all romance novels were a waste of my time and intellect, until I rediscovered romance about four years ago. I discovered that romance <i>
  <b>can</b>
</i> be well-written AND highly enjoyable and entertaining.<br /><br />But this novel is an example of why I turned up my nose at the genre 25 years ago.<br /><br />Life is too short to waste on drivel. I can see where this book is going from 1200 miles away. <br /><br />Four friends are in a bar having a HILARIOUS good time. OMG. Men suck. Yeah, men are so sucky. What kind of man would you want if you could have THE PERFECT MAN? OMG. Don't talk like that. You're insane. No, really. What's the perfect man? No. You're taking it too far. Heheheheheheh. Funny stuff. Seriously. Okay, he would definitely have to be faithful. Seriously? Really. Well, if you think so. Yeah, that's MOST important. What about a sense of humor? OMG. You are SO right. A sense of humor. OMG that's funny. Teehee. He should be good looking. Teehee. He should be great in bed. Teehee. He should be rich. Teehee. He should be responsible. DUDES!!! This is all so original and FUNNY. Seriously though? He should have a ten inch penis. <br /><br />Hmmmm.....where does the story go?....hmmm...I already know this is a murder suspense romance. The next door neighbor is a cop.....hmmm.....there is a serial killer and the title is Mr. Perfect....hmmmm.....nah, not predictable at all. I really have no idea what could possibly happen next. Oh, are the friends going to be murdered one by one? By a serial killer that heard about their original requirements for a man? Or something to that effect? WHATEVER. I seriously don't care.<br /><br />This is an example of severely dumbed down writing. Romance readers are idiots, right? Otherwise they would read serious literature instead of romance trash. Obviously romance readers can't handle big words or nuanced narratives. And of course, grammatical integrity, consistent voice and a plot that takes more thought than a infant can muster would just be TOO MUCH for a romance reader to handle.<br /><br />EXCERPT:<br /><br /><blockquote>Why on earth her mother had wanted <i>her</i> to baby-sit the cat, instead of Shelley or Dave, was beyond her. They both had kids who could play with BooBoo and keep him entertained. Since school was out for summer vacation, that meant someone was home at both their houses almost all day, every day.<br /><br />But, <i>nooo</i>. Jaine had to keep BooBoo. Never mind that she was single, was at work five days a week, and wasn't used to having a pet. If she did have a pet, it wouldn't be one like BooBook, anyway. He'd been in a feline pout ever since he'd been neutered, and he took out his frustration on the furniture. In just one week, he had frayed the sofa to the point that she would have to have it reupholstered.<br /><br />And BooBoo didn't like her. He like her well enough when he was in <i>his</i> home, coming around to be petted, but he didn't like being in her home at all. Every time she tried to pet him now, he arched his back and hissed at her.<br /><br />To top it off, Shelley was mad at her because Mom had chosen Jaine to baby-sit her precious BooBoo. After all, Shelley was the oldest, and obviously more settled. It didn't make sense that Jaine had been chosen over her. Jaine agree with her, but that didn't soothe the hurt feelings.<br /><br />No, what really topped it off was that David, who was a year younger than Shelley, was mad at her too. Not because of BooBoo; David was allergic to cats, No, what had him steamed was that Dad had stored his precious car in her garage--which meant <i>she</i> couldn't park in her own garage, since it was a single, and it was damned inconvenient. She wished David had the blasted car. She Wished Dad had left it in his own garage, but he'd been afraid to leave it unattended for six weeks. She understood that, but she didn't understand why she'd been chosen to baby-sit both cat and car. Shelley didn't understand the cat, David didn't understand the car, and Jaine didn't understand any of it.</blockquote><br /><br />You and me BOTH Jaine! I don't understand the purpose of the entire passage. <br /><br />Is this an obvious set-up for future happenings in the plot? The cat will be murdered and the car destroyed? <br /><br />Is this a pathetic attempt at characterization? Because now I hate Jaine and think she's a whiny baby. I feel no accord with this character.<br /><br />Or was this merely an attempt to pad the word count?<br /><br />It was all so stilted. Unnecessary. Like a conversation with someone who gives you way too many details about a story they're about to tell and you're just sitting there thinking: "Please get on with it. For the love of God--please."</span>
  <a data-text-id="9045131196174131044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_439197124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/439197124" />
    <a title="Geri Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads"><img alt="Geri Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487874758p2/11757728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/439197124?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geri Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geri Reads" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11725217-mr-perfect">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Carol Sanchez, Leilani Villanueva</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11757728-geri-reads?shelf=authors-who-disappointed-me">authors-who-disappointed-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer439197124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2412524236903888577"><br/><br/><b>5 (Still) Perfect Stars!!</b><br/><br/><b>Re-read time June 19 to 21 2013.</b><br/><br/>Still perfect after all this time. I've reread this book more than I could count and it never fails to make me laugh, cry and swoon. This book is what made me a fan of Linda Howard's writing. This was Linda Howard at her peak writing form; witty, fun, hilarious and terrifying at the same time. <br/><br/>Mr. Perfect is a story about four friends and their idea of Mr. Perfect. The fours friends understood, of course, that Mr. Perfect doesn't really ex</span>
  <span id="freeText2412524236903888577" style="display:none"><br /><br /><b>5 (Still) Perfect Stars!!</b><br /><br /><b>Re-read time June 19 to 21 2013.</b><br /><br />Still perfect after all this time. I've reread this book more than I could count and it never fails to make me laugh, cry and swoon. This book is what made me a fan of Linda Howard's writing. This was Linda Howard at her peak writing form; witty, fun, hilarious and terrifying at the same time. <br /><br />Mr. Perfect is a story about four friends and their idea of Mr. Perfect. The fours friends understood, of course, that Mr. Perfect doesn't really exist in real life but that didn't stop them from making the Mr. Perfect list. It was supposed to stay between them but one thing led to another and suddenly, the ladies find themselves as the newest national sensation. Worst of all, they also attracted the attention of a very disturb and sinister mind who will stop at nothing to hurt them. As to who and why he'd want to hurt them, well, I say, you must read the book because I'm not spoiling anything. :D<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Why I love this book...</u>
</b><br /><br />We're all familiar with that book where the heroine meets the hero and it was viola! Instant attraction, lust and even love at first sight. And then we get a heroine who keeps saying in her head, "He's so gorgeous," or "he's the most beautiful man I've ever met," or "he's perfect I wanna devour him." That plus the gushing and clenching their girly parts. <br /><br />This book doesn't have that. You'd get the exact opposite. First of all, Jaine (that's our female MC) thinks that Sam (our male MC) is foul-tempered drunk and a world-class jerk. No ifs and buts about it. She wasn't a bit attracted to him. In fact she contemplated on boiling her fingers because it touched him. :D <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>All she knew was that he was a rough-looking character, and he didn’t seem to hold down a regular job. At best, he was a drunk, and drunks could be mean and destructive. At worst, he was involved in illegal stuff, which added dangerous to the list. He was a big, muscular guy, with dark hair cut so short he almost looked like a skinhead. Every time she had seen him, he looked as if he hadn’t shaved in two or three days. Add that to the bloodshot eyes and bad temper, and she came up with drunk.</blockquote>
</i><br /> <br />It was downright hilarious the moment they "officially" met too. And boy, was Jaine ever wrong about her first impression of the guy. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I haven’t had any sleep, any breakfast, or any coffee. I’d better leave before I hurt you.” <br /><br />He nodded. “That’s a good idea. I’d hate to have to arrest you.” <br /><br />She stared at him, taken aback. “What?” <br /><br />“I’m a cop,” he said, then turned and walked back into his house. Jaine stared after him, shocked. A cop? <br /><br />“Well, fuck,” she said.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />See, what I mean? That was just refreshing to me. I always find it fascinating when a romance author tries to subvert a well known trope, in this case the insta-attraction or insta-lust trope, and give us something different.<br /><br />Of course, this dislike turned into something a lot more pleasant when Jaine saw Sam in his birthday suit outside her kitchen window. Jaine's inner monologue in that one was seriously funny and seriously hot. I swear reading that part made me wish, I had a hunky neighbor I could perv on. LH described Sam's nakedness and Jaine's reaction to it in way that make you laugh and turn you on at the same time. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>What then happened wasn’t her fault. She was standing at the sink rinsing out her cup when the kitchen light in the house across the way flicked on and Sam walked into view. She stopped breathing. Her lungs seized, and she stopped breathing. “Sweet baby Jesus,” she croaked, and managed to inhale.<br /><br />She was seeing more of Sam than she had ever thought she would; everything, in fact. He stood in front of the refrigerator, stark naked. She barely had time to admire his buns before he took a bottle of orange juice from the fridge, twisting off the top and tilting it to his mouth as he turned around. She forgot all about his buns. He was more impressive coming – no pun intended – than he was going, and that was saying something, because his butt was severely cute. The man was hung.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />In spite of that encounter, they didn't immediately jump into bed and have sex. They had to work out some issues first, plus the fact there was a killer on the loose after Jaine and her friends. But when they did? YOWZA! LH writes some of the best love scenes around. She's not overly descriptive. There's almost like a brusque quality to the way she writes these scenes that does something your imagination. And for someone with a very active imagination like moi, this was just perfect for me.<br /><br />Sam Donovan, or as Jaine referred to him as the jerk, was a wonderfully swoony character. He is alpha without being too over the top and the jerk is funny. He can totally match Jaine in the wit department. Plus, he ain't that bad looking either. Oh, who am I kidding? Sam is gorgeous in a totally manly way and most of all, he's got the right equipment. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I tracked it down on the Web. It was funny stuff – Ms. C.” She gaped at him. “How did you know?” she demanded. <br />He snorted. “Like I wouldn’t recognize your smart-ass mouth even in print. ‘Anything over eight is strictly for show-and-tell’,” he quoted at her.<br /> “I might have known you’d remember only the sex stuff.” <br />“Sex is much on my mind these days. And just for the record – I don’t have anything for show-and-tell.” <br />If he didn’t, he hadn’t missed it by much, Jaine thought, remembering with great fondness how he had looked in profile. <br />He continued, “I’m just happy I’m not in the point-and-laugh category.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The story was seamlessly told in multiple POVs, with Jaine having the most of them. We also get to be inside the mind of the killer and let me tell you, it was creepy as hell and very disturbing. I have to warn you though, there is much sadness that happened in this book. I won't elaborate anything more than that but this book isn't all hearts and rainbows. But it does have an HEA.<br /><br />Overall, very solid and pretty much unforgettable story from Linda Howard. Definitely worth the five stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2412524236903888577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who enjoyes  fun, contemporary romantic suspense novels. </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=cops-detectives-agents">cops-detectives-agents</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=contemporary-romantic-suspense">contemporary-romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=disquised-incognito-undercover">disquised-incognito-undercover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=illness-mental">illness-mental</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=murder">murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=sizzzzzle">sizzzzzle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108691762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8936286932757972457"><br/>What do you get when four friends get together for their weekly girls night out and have a little too much to drink? Well, in this story, you get a list detailing what these friends think it takes to make the perfect man. <br/><br/>And what do you get when that list becomes an overnight sensation with a nearly cult like following? Well, in this story, you get murder!<br/><br/>I’ve had this book on my shelves for quite awhile and whenever my Goodreads friends would talk about Linda Howard’s books, <i>Mr. Perfect</i> was su</span>
  <span id="freeText8936286932757972457" style="display:none"><br />What do you get when four friends get together for their weekly girls night out and have a little too much to drink? Well, in this story, you get a list detailing what these friends think it takes to make the perfect man. <br /><br />And what do you get when that list becomes an overnight sensation with a nearly cult like following? Well, in this story, you get murder!<br /><br />I’ve had this book on my shelves for quite awhile and whenever my Goodreads friends would talk about Linda Howard’s books, <i>Mr. Perfect</i> was sure to be listed as one of her very best, and almost always a favorite. So why did I put off reading this book, you ask? Because I thought the cover was ugly. And let me just tell you now, it’s true what they say; you should never judge a book by its cover.<br /><br /><i>Mr. Perfect </i> was a fun, fast paced, sexy read and once I got started I just couldn’t put it down. And while the idea that such a list could become so insanely popular and cause such havoc is a bit on the farfetched side, the story was written in such a way that made it believable, and the characters were written just as well. <br /><br />Jaine Bright and Sam Donovan were both so perfect, and yet so flawed that they felt like real people to me, not just words and images bunched together to give us characters to read about, but honest to goodness real people. Their banter was laugh out loud funny and their sexual chemistry burned up the pages.<br /><br />I also loved the secondary characters who filled out the group of friends, four ladies working for the same company yet in different departments. Their love for each other was so apparent, and it made me think of a couple of my own closest friends. I could easily see us all sitting down and getting carried away, laughing and just having a great time creating our ideal man, our own Mr. Perfect. <br /><br />The bottom line – This was my first Linda Howard read and before I was even 1/3 of the way through I was ordering more of her books. It was fun, exciting and very sexy, so needless to say, I really enjoyed <i>Mr. Perfect</i> and I’m looking forward to reading more by this author!<br /><br /><b>4.5/5.0</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8936286932757972457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Sam sure is sexy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443597410i/16383838._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Jaine is a great heroine. Has a temper, has a backbone, has a sense of humour.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“If you're looking for Mr. Perfect, you‟re going to spend your whole life being disappointed, because he doesn‟t exist. You have to get the best deal you can, but there will always be problems.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br>And that is where all the trouble started. With "the List"!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443597410i/16383841.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443597410i/16383839._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443597410i/16383840.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I told you, we haven't had sex! It was just a kiss."<br>Like the Viper was just a car, and Mount Everest was just a hill.” </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443597498i/16383846._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2153583310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2153583310" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2153583310?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with">girls-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2153583310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11278273696450750210"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508100627i/24182214._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Jaine works in an office with a bunch of computer nerds who provide us with some slightly funny signs on the elevators each morning.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“FIRST YOU PILLAGE, THEN YOU BURN. THOSE WHO DO NOT COMPLY WILL BE SUSPENDED FROM THE RAIDING TEAM.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>That was the funniest one, in my opinion, but I like nerdy gamer stuff sometimes, and it only got a tiny half-smile out of me. No lol-ing.<br/><br/>What also didn't make me Lol was when Jaine gets together with three of her friends and they write a list describing what wou</span>
  <span id="freeText11278273696450750210" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508100627i/24182214._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jaine works in an office with a bunch of computer nerds who provide us with some slightly funny signs on the elevators each morning.<br><br><b>
  <i>“FIRST YOU PILLAGE, THEN YOU BURN. THOSE WHO DO NOT COMPLY WILL BE SUSPENDED FROM THE RAIDING TEAM.” </i>
</b><br><br>That was the funniest one, in my opinion, but I like nerdy gamer stuff sometimes, and it only got a tiny half-smile out of me. No lol-ing.<br><br>What also didn't make me Lol was when Jaine gets together with three of her friends and they write a list describing what would be their perfect man. I guess it just seemed kind of lame to me. Why would they write it down? Plus, they were described as laughing so hard through it that they were disturbing other tables at the restaurant, but I just didn't find it that funny. It was okay, but not hilarious. *shrugs*<br><br>What did make me laugh was her interactions with her hot neighbor, Sam. Those were very funny cute-meet moments, and Sam was definitely adorable and funny.<br><br><b>
  <i>At the moment, he kinda knew how the male praying mantis felt when he<br>was approaching Ms. Mantis, knowing the sex was going to be great but he was going to get his head bitten off.<br>Ah, well. Some things were worth losing your head.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508100627i/24182216.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> So this written "list" gets picked up by an office worker who prints it in their newsletter, which somehow makes it to a local news station who talks about it as a human-interest story, and then comes to national attention via an employee with a sister who works at Good Morning America.<br><br>Craziness ensues.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508100628i/24182217._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The price of fame.<br><br>And the other price of fame? Psychotic killers who decide they don't like your list and that they are going to kill you all. I hate when that happens.<br><br>The mystery in this book is actually pretty good. I figured it out, but I thought it was clever enough. The romance is completely insta-love, but cute. The h and H are both great characters as well. The only drawback was the cheesiness and also the cut-out characters of her friends. This would be a good beach read if you are the type that goes outdoors. For me, it was a good comfy-chair-late-at-night read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508100627i/24182215._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11278273696450750210" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397897919?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397897919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11583592389775137143"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443464524i/16363248._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well, that's three for three for Linda Howard! Another winner. I read a few reviews before I started this one, so my expectations were high. And I wasn't the least bit disappointed! <br/><br/>A few people had a hard time with the <i>insta-love</i> between Jaine and Sam, but for some reason it didn't bother me a bit. In fact I felt it added to Sam's incredible charm and cocky appeal. He knew what he wanted, and he didn't waste any time playing games. What's not to love about that? <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443464524i/16363249._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I have to admit, I have a</span>
  <span id="freeText11583592389775137143" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443464524i/16363248._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, that's three for three for Linda Howard! Another winner. I read a few reviews before I started this one, so my expectations were high. And I wasn't the least bit disappointed! <br><br>A few people had a hard time with the <i>insta-love</i> between Jaine and Sam, but for some reason it didn't bother me a bit. In fact I felt it added to Sam's incredible charm and cocky appeal. He knew what he wanted, and he didn't waste any time playing games. What's not to love about that? <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443464524i/16363249._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I have to admit, I have a serious girl-crush on Jaine. She was so mouthy and sarcastic. A girl after my own heart. She also didn't even try to fight off the strong feelings she had for Sam. No head games here. Just a straight shooter. They were perfect together. <br> <br><br><b>
  <i>"I don't know how serious it is," she said, knowing she was lying. <br>"I'm not rushing into anything." <br>For her part, she couldn't get much more serious. <br>She was in love with the big jerk. <br>Exactly how or what he felt was still open for discussion.</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443464524i/16363250.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The story was very suspenseful. The killer was one sick individual. And that final showdown... wow! The last 10% of the book was so intense, I didn't even remember turning the pages. <br><br>Fabulous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11583592389775137143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_796756874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/796756874" />
    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/796756874?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=tragic-loss">tragic-loss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer796756874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1286470077149587489">~~~~ 4 STARS OR 7.5-8/10 ~~~~<br/><br/>Despite being released years ago, the books I've read by Linda Howard are so evocative and sexy that some newer books honestly can't compete. This is the third book by LH I've read so far but after the first, she became one of my favourite authors. Romantic suspense when written well is fantastic. <br/>I loved the suspense here, it had me stumped till past half way through when I realized I was making a grave error in my assumptions. <br/><br/>The disturbing nature of the crimes co</span>
  <span id="freeText1286470077149587489" style="display:none">~~~~ 4 STARS OR 7.5-8/10 ~~~~<br /><br />Despite being released years ago, the books I've read by Linda Howard are so evocative and sexy that some newer books honestly can't compete. This is the third book by LH I've read so far but after the first, she became one of my favourite authors. Romantic suspense when written well is fantastic. <br />I loved the suspense here, it had me stumped till past half way through when I realized I was making a grave error in my assumptions. <br /><br />The disturbing nature of the crimes committed were riveting and I was horrified by the inner workings of the killers mind. We get several pov's here, with the majority being Janie's, the heroine. Reading this was like solving an intelligent puzzle and I really enjoyed it.<br />The romance was sweet but the sensuality was RAW. It's hard to write like that when tackling love scenes. But instead of drawn out sex scenes and verbal catalysts, LH zeroes in on the sexual sensuality between people. Her sexy time is short but packs an intensity no lengthy and drawn out sex scene can ever accomplish.<br />I know I've mentioned this in previous reviews of her books, but when it's that good it deserves mentioning all over again. I loved how laid back and confident Sam was. With the Mr. Perfect list causing a huge controversy for men all over, Sam seemed to find the whole thing amusing and not at all demeaning. That's a man in charge of himself and confident in his abilities!<br /><br />There was a scene early on when Jaine catches Sam in his kitchen, naked, chugging back a container of milk. Instead of being embarrassed or scandalized, he relished in the ability to shock her and advertise exactly what she's been missing. Honestly, it was hot, and from then on I developed a respect for him and his security in being a real man.<br /><br />The only thing I found puzzling was the speed in which Sam and Jaine progressed in their relationship. It felt too insta love-ish. But even considering that, I loved their interaction and enjoyed the story very much. <br />The ending was edge-on-your-seat good, with the killer finally reaching a desperate precipice. I loved it. If you haven't read LH before, start now!! My fave remains to be 'After The Night'.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1286470077149587489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10445878992724808862">I cannot praise this book enough: brilliant, fantastic, amazing, awesome - yes, I do realize these are all synonyms. <br/>This is the best book I've read by Linda Howard, so far that is. I wish to recommend it to all my friends.<br/><br/>Mr.Perfect not only assures you to have a great time, but you can also be sure that once you start reading this book, the pages will turn like there is no tomorrow. This is hilarious, it completely took me by surprise, as I was not expecting to laugh so much. The mystery and t</span>
  <span id="freeText10445878992724808862" style="display:none">I cannot praise this book enough: brilliant, fantastic, amazing, awesome - yes, I do realize these are all synonyms. <br />This is the best book I've read by Linda Howard, so far that is. I wish to recommend it to all my friends.<br /><br />Mr.Perfect not only assures you to have a great time, but you can also be sure that once you start reading this book, the pages will turn like there is no tomorrow. This is hilarious, it completely took me by surprise, as I was not expecting to laugh so much. The mystery and thriller the chills, a book usually doesn't make me react like this, but this one sure did. The romance is out of this world, both main characters are just so perfect for each other, it also helped the fact that they couldn't stand each other, I'm especially in love with love/hate relationships - you have to admit it always makes things more interesting when they unfold.<br /><br />Linda Howard did everything right while writing this book, for this book is a master-piece and has won a very-well deserved place on my favorites list. - Unforgettable!</span>

<div id="review_1713271079" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713271079" />
    <a title="Naksed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed"><img alt="Naksed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417804998p2/29458352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713271079?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naksed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naksed" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed">Naksed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713271079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8313650539155089157">I had the same issue with Linda Howard's <i>Mr. Perfect</i> as I did with her <i>Mackenzie's Mountain</i>. I loved the protagonists but I hated the story. Very tough to rate this one.<br/><br/>The banter between the two was some of the best I read from LH. Jaine is a quirky, feisty, thoroughly modern and very likable woman. When she starts sparring with her grumpy but oh so sexy next door neighbor, Detective Sam Donovan, I felt like I could get a tub of popcorn and just sit there watching them exchange insults, flirtat</span>
  <span id="freeText8313650539155089157" style="display:none">I had the same issue with Linda Howard's <i>Mr. Perfect</i> as I did with her <i>Mackenzie's Mountain</i>. I loved the protagonists but I hated the story. Very tough to rate this one.<br /><br />The banter between the two was some of the best I read from LH. Jaine is a quirky, feisty, thoroughly modern and very likable woman. When she starts sparring with her grumpy but oh so sexy next door neighbor, Detective Sam Donovan, I felt like I could get a tub of popcorn and just sit there watching them exchange insults, flirtations, and hot kisses all day long.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Tell me something,”</b>
</i> he asks her after she got herself into yet another predicament, <i>
  <b>"Is there ever a day when you don’t pick a fight?” <br /><br />“The days when I don’t see you,”</b>
</i> she shoots right back at him.<br /><br />Later, when she catches him strutting naked in his kitchen, her first thought is to run right over to his house <i>
  <b>"to audition as his mattress."<br /><br />"Don’t kiss me,”</b>
</i> she warns him on their next encounter, even though that's exactly what she wants him to do.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"I don’t intend to ,”</b>
</i> he quips, <i>
  <b>I don’t have my whip and chair with me."</b>
</i><br /><br />And so on and so forth. So why did I not rate this book higher, when it had me chuckling at almost every page? It was the "suspense" part of this "romantic suspense" story that ruined it for me.<br /><br />The plot is centered on a woman-hating serial killer who targets Jaine and her close-knit group of friends because they made up a silly list of the attributes they would wish on an ideal man, a "Mr. Perfect", which became a viral national news interest story and sparked a kind of gender war between the women who rallied to their "sisters" and the men who were offended and disgusted by some of the items on the list.<br /><br />My problem is that it was very difficult for me to imagine that the list the ladies came up with would elicit any interest in the media or outrage people.<br /><br /> It was so tame, talking about how men should be faithful and have a sense of humor and at the end, that they should be good looking and good in bed, preferably with a ten inch penis. That's it. Hard to imagine Good Morning America and People Magazine descending on an obscure group of low level corporate employees who were simply having a laugh at happy hour and give them their fifteen minutes of fame based on a tame list like this Sorry, just didn't buy it.<br /><br />As for the psycho who goes after them because they offended his sensibilities with their crude, vulgar, whorish ways, he was suc a cartoon character, Frankensteined from various, equally buffoonish villains featured on popular crime/horror movies and TV shows like <i>Psycho, Silence of the Lambs, Dressed to Kill</i> or <i>Law &amp; Order.</i><br /><br />I really enjoy LH' signature witty and sexy banter but this story has not aged well (one scene has the detective patiently wait for thirty minutes for a file to download from his email to his computer lol, characters struggle with cell phones, etc.) and its cringe-inducing shortcomings eventually marred my enjoyment of two hot, funny, and likable characters. Can we please revive Jaine and Sam and plunk them down in a worthy story?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8313650539155089157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12580514?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammy" href="/user/show/785960-tammy">Tammy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/785960-tammy?shelf=keepers">keepers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/785960-tammy?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/785960-tammy?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12580514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1022990572801400858">Remember the discussion thread on Amazon several months ago where the boardies discussed their favorite lines in a book? Now I finally understand the popular line ... "I'm not holding you against your will; I'm holding you against your car." <br/><br/>This book was full of verbal sparring between Jaine Bright and her neighbor, Detective Sam Donovan, that was downright hilarious at times. Jaine first meets Sam when she accidentally backs over his metal garbage can with her new Viper. Tempers flare as these</span>
  <span id="freeText1022990572801400858" style="display:none">Remember the discussion thread on Amazon several months ago where the boardies discussed their favorite lines in a book? Now I finally understand the popular line ... "I'm not holding you against your will; I'm holding you against your car." <br /><br />This book was full of verbal sparring between Jaine Bright and her neighbor, Detective Sam Donovan, that was downright hilarious at times. Jaine first meets Sam when she accidentally backs over his metal garbage can with her new Viper. Tempers flare as these two discover a strong, immediate attraction that they both try to deny. Their first kiss takes place when Jaine is washing her car - no spoilers here! - but it is one of the funniest and sexiest that I have ever read.<br /><br />The storyline of the four friends and their silly list of qualifications for Mr. Perfect makes for a nice secondary plot. However, a creepy character committing two, gruesome murders as a result of the list was overly familiar to me - it reminded me of a movie that I once saw. But all in all, I loved this book! I'm not sure why I let it sit in my TBR pile for so long, but I highly recommend it and I may re-read it myself just for grins and giggles.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer369644928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9255631132343951103"><i>Perfection</i> is the name of this book! I was up till 5:30 in the morning finishing this and when I got to the end I wanted more, more Jaine and Sam. I loved the romance and wanted so much more. Jaine was a firecracker and I loved her. She was soo kick-ass and knew cars and didn't mind speaking her mind and throwing herself in the fray.<br/><br/>She just bought a house, her siblings are miffed with her since her vacation parents left their cat and her dad's prized car in her possession. She also thinks her n</span>
  <span id="freeText9255631132343951103" style="display:none"><i>Perfection</i> is the name of this book! I was up till 5:30 in the morning finishing this and when I got to the end I wanted more, more Jaine and Sam. I loved the romance and wanted so much more. Jaine was a firecracker and I loved her. She was soo kick-ass and knew cars and didn't mind speaking her mind and throwing herself in the fray.<br /><br />She just bought a house, her siblings are miffed with her since her vacation parents left their cat and her dad's prized car in her possession. She also thinks her neighbour is a drunk boor, proof he is dressed badly, comes in late and always looks hungover and then she finds out is because he is a cop on a task force. They have the most <i>hilarious</i> and sexy encounters. Sam has a habit of sneaking up on her and she has a habit of using a lot of cuss words and they have a hilarious conversation about eggs.<br /><br />On a Friday night after work, she and her friends make a list of Mr Perfect and that list goes public and viral bringing a lot of attention to them and a psycho killer. One of the friends gets murdered and so does another one later. The mystery and romance are perfectly blended. This is pure vintage Linda Howard at her best. I loved the romance, despite being whirlwind it worked for me. Even the fights between Jaine and Sam were sexy. Jaine had been anti-men since by the age of 23 she had three broken engagements under her belt but with Sam there was instant fire between them.<br /><br />I so didn't want this book to end.<br /></span>

<div id="review_449995078" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449995078" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/449995078?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=heroines-i-love">heroines-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=comfort-read">comfort-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=feel-good-read">feel-good-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449995078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9893665366539642311"><blockquote>
  <i>“Tell me something,” he said conversationally, strolling beside her as she stalked, as best as she was able, to her car. “Is there ever a day when you don’t pick a fight?”<br/>“The days when I don’t see you,” she shot back.</i>
</blockquote> <p>I have read many books, and this book is still the book with the best bantering between the hero and the heroine. I LOVE this book, have re-read it many times, and it’s still one of my favorite books of all time. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>It was a good thing she was off men, or she really might hav</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText9893665366539642311" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Tell me something,” he said conversationally, strolling beside her as she stalked, as best as she was able, to her car. “Is there ever a day when you don’t pick a fight?”<br />“The days when I don’t see you,” she shot back.</i>
</blockquote> <p>I have read many books, and this book is still the book with the best bantering between the hero and the heroine. I LOVE this book, have re-read it many times, and it’s still one of my favorite books of all time. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>It was a good thing she was off men, or she really might have charged across the two driveways and right up to his kitchen door. But off men or not, she still appreciated art, and her neighbour was a work of art, hovering somewhere between classic Grecian statue and porn star.</i>
</blockquote> <p>Janie is the perfect heroine. She’s sassy and feisty and so funny. I just loved her. She recently bought her first house, and she loves everything about it, except for her rude neighbour, who must be a drunk and busy with illegal activities because of his blood shot eyes, dirty clothes and the unusual hours he comes home. But then she finds out he’s a cop, and things gets very interesting between them. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>She attacked life, rather than simply letting it happen; he’d never before met anyone so annoying and funny and sharp. He had major plans for her, the most immediate of which was getting her under him. No way would he let anything happen to her, even if he had to quit his job and become her twenty-four-hour-a-day bodyguard.</i>
</blockquote> <p>Sam is the perfect hero. He’s brash, confident, so sexy and not shy at all. He’s a cop that works strange hours, trying to work on his house in his spare time, and his new neighbour has something against him getting sleep. But after another heated encounter, he can’t help but notice the very strong and hard effect his feisty neighbour has on him. </p> <p>But then the list that Janie and her three friends drunkenly made of the Perfect Man, suddenly becomes famous, and triggers the attention of a killer, who is set on killing the ladies of the list. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I always heard that sex was different with a woman you loved, but I didn’t believe it. Sex was sex. Then I got inside you and it was like sticking my cock in an electrical outlet.”<br />“Oh. Was that what all that shaking and yelling was about?” She sniffled, but she was paying attention.<br />“Smart-ass. Yeah, that’s what it was about, not that I was the only one doing some shaking and yelling. It was different. Hotter. Stronger. And when it was over, I wanted to do it all over again.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <p>The romance was FANTASTIC!! I loved the hilarious banter between Janie and Sam, their scorching attraction, and the fact that the more time they spent together the more they wanted to be in each other’s company. These two are one of the most perfect couples ever. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>“I kept you from sleeping? I kept <b>you</b> from sleeping?” he repeated incredulously. “You are the same woman who shook me out of a sound sleep at two A.M. yesterday morning, aren’t you?”<br />“I didn’t shake you. I kind of bounced on you, but I didn’t shake you.”<br />“Bounced,” he repeated.<br />“You had a hard-on. I couldn’t let it go to waste, could I?”<br />“You could have woke me up before you started not letting it go to waste.”<br />“Look,” she said, exasperated, “if you don’t want it used, don’t lie on your back with it sticking up like that. If that isn’t an invitation, I don’t know what is.”</i>
</blockquote> <p>And the sexy times …. HOT DAMN!! The sparks flying between these two were AWESOME and just explosive!!!! </p> <blockquote>
  <i>“Is it possible for men to have PMS?”<br />“They don’t need it,” Jaine said, thinking of her jerk of a neighbour – a cop jerk. “They’re born with testosterone poisoning.”</i>
</blockquote> <p>Janie’s group of friends were just fantastic and hilarious, and I loved them. </p> <p>As always Linda Howard writes an intriguing plot, and I loved trying to figure out who the killer was. </p> <p>I love this author, and this book is one of my favorites. If you love hilarious banter between main characters, a romance that is so hot it will burn your fingers and a very suspenseful plot, this is the book for you. <b>HIGHLY RECOMMENDED</b>.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="9893665366539642311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
